text:
I told my husband I had been experimenting with new salad dressing recipes. I made a new honey mustard dressing. He warned me he was not a "honey mustard" kind of guy. I served it on a main dish salad with lettuce greens, chopped bell pepper, carrot, celery, and sauteed turkey breast, all topped with toasted almonds. It was fantastic. After he licked the bowl, I asked him how he liked the honey mustard dressing. He asked, "That was honey mustard?" He loved it. This incredibly easy recipe will be a staple in our house. I used dijon mustard and low fat mayo from Trader Joes.

text:
It's Stone Crab Claw season in SW Florida and we are really taking advantage of it!  These delights demand a classic honey mustard dipping sauce and I was in the mood to try something different than what I usually make, "Honey Mustard Sauce," also from this site.  This recipe, "Honey Mustard Dressing II,"  calls for yellow mustard rather than the Dijon in the other recipe, and this recipe calls for a little lemon juice, where the other does not.  I loved this!  It's neither too sweet, mustard-y nor mayonnaise-y.  Just perfect.  Hubs, however, wasn't quite as enthusiastic.  He said this wasn't bad, but he prefers the other.  In the final analysis, both are very good.

This is REALLY good !!!  I quadruple the recipe every time I make it and keep it in a mason jar in the fridge.   If I needed to stress anything, it would be not to use your ordinary, cheap yellow mustard.  Amp it up a bit and use an artisan mustard...it makes a HUGE difference.   Fabulous on a salad, but really good as a dip with fried chicken strips, etc.  I used a smidge more lemon juice to 'brighten' up the flavor a bit, too.  This recipe is a keeper !

I've been looking for a copycat recipe of O'Charley's honey mustard dressing and this recipe is the closest I've come.

I used Mr. Kensington's mayo that is made with sunflower oil rather than soybean oil. I used Dijon mustard and the honey and lemon juice as stated in the recipe. The end result was heavy on the mayonnaise flavor, so I added a bit of yellow mustard and a little bit more honey.  It was very good, definitely much better than what I had been using. I will keep this recipe as my go to recipe. Its so simple and yummy, you cant beat it!)

text:
Excellent as written. The mustard taste is subtle but noticeable and we enjoyed the sweetness and creaminess of this.  Then again, we add cranberries, apples, and candied pecans to our salads often, so this just complements that.  You should adjust the sweetness according to what you are making it for.  I decided to make a honey mustard coleslaw with this . I made the dressing and then added onion juice (blitzing onions with a drizzle of water in my blender) to the finished slaw after the honey mustard dressing had been mixed in.   This is a keeper for our family.  ----- Note: do NOT use salad dressing / miracle whip.  Not the same and the flavor difference is night and day.  Be sure that you use plain mayo like the recipe is referring to otherwise the flavor of it will simply obliterate the rest of the flavors.

Great.  Easy.  Quick.  Delicious.  My go to salad dressing.  I always add a healthy dose of extra virgin olive oil.  It thins out the dressing so it's not so concentrated and makes it a bit easier to coat the vegetables.  I find it too strong otherwise.    We also use honey mustard instead of mustard, and don't use mayonaisse, but a whipped dressing.  (Since that's what's on hand.)  Very good!

I made this the other day with the correct measurements for 9 servings and it tasted like I had just made a bowl of mustard tinted mayonnaise. I had to add a lot more mustard (approx. 1/3 cup or more total) and several tablespoons more of honey before it even tasted like normal honey mustard. After all the hard work and refrigerating overnight it tasted delicious! I would highly recommend this recipe, just be prepared to add more honey and mustard.

This is a great recipe that I will definitely make again.
